The Conservatives plan to create 16,000 new apprenticeships and three million training places, aiming to hold apprenticeships on par with degrees. Labour has pledged to create 80,000 more apprenticeships, with 33,000 coming from the High Speed 2 rail line project, and promises apprenticeships to every school leaver who "gets the grades." The Liberal Democrats want to expand apprenticeships and develop national colleges for vocational skills, aiming to end the "snobbery" about apprenticeships. UKIP plans to introduce an option for students to take an apprenticeship instead of four non-core GCSE subjects, while scrapping tuition fees for some students taking degrees in high-demand vocational subjects. The Green Party plans to expand apprenticeships by increasing funding and providing an apprenticeship to all qualified young people aged 16-25 who want one. The SNP has pledged to provide 125,000 "modern" apprenticeships in the next parliament and offer a place on a training or learning scheme to every 16 to 19-year-old in the country who's out of work or training. Express and TNT, have also introduced additional charges on shipments between the UK and the EU to reflect the increased investment they have had to make in adjusting their systems to cope with Brexit.  The article highlights the changes in VAT rules brought in by HM Revenue and Customs on 1 January. Under these new rules, VAT is now collected at the point of sale rather than at the point of importation. This means that overseas retailers sending goods to the UK are expected to register for UK VAT and account for it to HMRC if the sale value is less than €150 (£135). The government spokesperson explains that the new VAT model ensures goods from EU and non-EU countries are treated in the same way and that UK businesses are not disadvantaged by competition from VAT-free imports.  Campaigner Richard Allen, founder of Retailers Against VAT Abuse Schemes, points out that the massive increase in international online shopping has led to VAT evasion on a large scale. The new HMRC rules are aimed at tackling this issue, but it is unclear how firms who fail to register for UK VAT will be dealt with. Dutch Bike Bits, in particular, has expressed their dissatisfaction with the new VAT model, stating that it would result in ludicrous fees for companies worldwide if every country adopted the same idea. Cory also added definitions of connive, a synonym of the verb collude, including "to deliberately ignore" and "to turn a blind eye." The first police ombudsman for Northern Ireland, Nuala O'Loan, adopted the definitions of Stevens and Cory, concluding that there had been collusion in the murder of Raymond McCord jnr. However, her successor as police ombudsman, Al Hutchinson, applied a less broad definition in his report on the attack on McGurk's Bar. In the report, he wrote that the essence of collusion requires that a number of elements be present, including an agreement between two or more parties and evidence that the act or omission complained of was deliberate. Irish judge Peter Smithwick gave a similar definition of collusion to that of Cory, stating that it generally means the commission of an act but can also involve an omission or failure to act.  In evaluating the quality of the output, it is important to note that the definitions provided by these individuals are diverse and cover a range of aspects related to collusion. However, some critical drawbacks in the model outputs are:  1. Lack of consistency: The definitions provided by different individuals are not entirely consistent with each other, which may lead to confusion and difficulties in understanding the concept of collusion. 2. Vagueness: Some definitions are quite broad and lack specificity, which may make it difficult to determine whether a particular action or omission constitutes collusion. 3. Focus on specific aspects: Some definitions focus on specific aspects of collusion, such as connivance or secret understandings, while others emphasize broader concepts like agreements or arrangements. 4. Ambiguity: Some definitions are ambiguous and may be open to interpretation, which could potentially lead to different conclusions in different cases.  In conclusion, the output provided in Output (a) is more comprehensive and consistent in its definitions of collusion compared to Output (b).
